ADDITIONAL NOTES
A. NOTES
Precipitation utiIized during winter months to meet forage freshwater requirements.
Irrigation weIls 12A(W), 13-4, 14-2, 14-4, 16-4 & 16-6 were non-operational in 2023. AIl weIls wiIl be sampIed once the weIls become operational and used
during the cropping season. Heavy rains during the winter season aIlowed for a greater amount of surface water aIlocation to grow crops.
FieId CVW 5 Cor had a lower than anticipated removal rate due to lower than anticipated N. This resuIted in fieId ratios sIightIy exceeding target limits.
FieIds 13-2 Wheat, 13-6 Wheat, 16-3 Wheat, 13-2 Sudan, 14-5 Corn, 15-1 Corn, 15-5B Corn, 15-7 Corn, CVW 4 Corn, 11-5 AIfaIfa, 13-12 AIfaIfa, 14-7 AIfaIfa,
14-9 AIfaIfa, 14-10 AIfaIfa, 16-1 AIfaIfa, & 16-6 AIfaIfa had higher than anticipated removal rates. This was due to higher than expected N and/or yieId. The YN
removed, which is based on anaIysis derived through a certified laboratory, exceeded the anticipated vaIues for this crop. Appropriate management practices
resuIted in decent yieIds and/or higher than expected nutrient removal rates.
Nutrients appIied to permanent crops, such as trees and vines, are used for tree growth, vine deveIopment and fruit production (grapes, nuts, etc.). Comparing
nutrient appIications to nutrient content of harvested material for permanent crops is not appropriate and wiIl resuIt in high fieId ratios. A more accurate reporting
methodoIogy wiIl need to be deveIoped in order to account for nutrients retained in the permanent crops. AIl appIications wiIl continue to be monitored cIoseIy to
ensure that over appIication of nutrients does not occur.
